          should: 1) preserve the original information as much as possible, with

          @doi:10.1101/2021.10.21.21265225; @pmid:31036433]", and 4) the revised
          paragraph must encapsulate the entire revision, following the C-C-C
          structure, within a single, cohesive paragraph.

          (TWAS), a powerful method that investigates associations between

          complex interactions within gene networks. Our study aims to address
          this gap by exploring the potential of integrating gene co-expression

          drug repurposing.

          In recent years, the abundance of gene expression data across various
          tissues has facilitated the development of transcription-wide
          association studies (TWAS) [@doi:10.1038/nbt.3838;

          various tissues has opened up new avenues for understanding complex
          biological processes and their relationships with human diseases. This
          has led to the development of transcription-wide association studies
          (TWAS), which integrate expression quantitative trait loci (eQTLs)

          manuscript aims to address this knowledge gap by exploring alternative
          approaches, such as gene co-expression networks and clustering of
          complex traits, which may provide a more comprehensive understanding
          of disease etiology and drug mechanisms, ultimately leading to the
          identification of novel therapeutic targets and improved drug
          repurposing strategies.

          [@doi:10.1186/s13059-021-02591-w] and drug repurposing
          [@doi:10.1038/nn.4618] endeavors, highlighting its potential in
          addressing current knowledge gaps in these areas.

          complex diseases at the transcriptome level and improving disease-risk
          prediction and drug repurposing, there remains a need to address the
          limitations of this approach by incorporating network-level
          interactions for a more comprehensive understanding of biological
          processes.

              @doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03751-6; @doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776;
              @doi:10.1186/s13040-020-00216-9]. A promising method to unravel
              the biological processes underlying these data is the
              transcription-wide association study (TWAS), which combines
              expression quantitative trait loci (eQTLs) data to offer a
              mechanistic explanation for genetic associations detected in
              genome-wide association studies (GWAS). TWAS investigates whether
              genetic variants' effects on human diseases are mediated by
              perturbations in gene regulatory mechanisms
              [@doi:10.1371/journal.pgen.1009482; @doi:10.1038/ng.3506;
              @doi:10.1371/journal.pgen.1007889; @doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. These
              approaches have significantly contributed to our understanding of
              disease etiology at the transcriptome level [@pmid:33931583;
              @doi:10.1101/2021.10.21.21265225; @pmid:31036433] and have been
              instrumental in disease-risk prediction (polygenic scores)
              [@doi:10.1186/s13059-021-02591-w] and drug repurposing
              [@doi:10.1038/nn.4618] endeavors. Nonetheless, TWAS's focus on
              individual genes fails to capture the complex interactions
              occurring at the network level, representing a notable knowledge
              gap in our current understanding of these biological processes.


              In this revised paragraph, I have maintained the original
              information while ensuring most references to scientific articles
              remain unchanged for academic integrity. The paragraph now follows
              the Context-Content-Conclusion (C-C-C) structure by setting the
              stage with the availability of gene expression data, summarizing
              what is known from the literature about TWAS and its applications,
              and highlighting the knowledge gap regarding complex interactions
              at the network level that the manuscript aims to address.
